\section{Cobordism}
\paragraph{} Here I follow to \cite{stong:cobord}.
\subsection{Cobordism categories}
\paragraph{} Let 

\begin{definition}\label{cobord_cat_defn}\cite{stong:cobord}
A \textit{cobordism category} $\left(\mathscr C, \partial, j\right)$ is a triple in which
\begin{enumerate}
	\item [(a)] $\mathscr C$ is a category having finite sums and an initial object;
	\item[(b)] $\partial:  \mathscr C \to \mathscr C$ is an additive  functor such that for each object $X$ of $\mathscr C$, $~\partial \partial \left( X\right)$ is an initial object;
	\item[(c)] $j :\partial \to \Id_{\mathscr C}$ is a natural transformation of additive from $\partial$ to the identity functor $\Id_{\mathscr C}$; and 
	\item[(d)] There is a small category $\Id_{\mathscr C_0}$ or $\Id_{\mathscr C}$ such that each object of $\mathscr C$ is isomorphic  to and object of $\mathscr C_0$
\end{enumerate} 
\end{definition}

\subsection{Chow ring and homology}

\subsubsection{Divisors and rational equivalence }
\paragraph{} 
Here I follow to \cite{fulton:intersection}, \cite{fulton:intro_intersection}

\paragraph{ Homology and cohomology}

A complex projective variety $\sX$ has homology groups $Hq\sX$ and cohomology 
groups $H^q\sX$. There are {\it cup 
	products }
\bean
H^p\sX \otimes H^q \sX \xrightarrow{\smile }  H^{p+ q} \sX
\eean
and {\it cap products} 
\bean
H^p\sX \otimes H_q \sX \xrightarrow{\frown }  H_{p+ q} \sX
\eean
which make $H^*\sX = \bigoplus \H^p\sX$ a skew-commutative graded ring, and $H_*\sX = \bigoplus \H_p\sX$ an $H^*\sX$ -module. If $f: \sX \to \sY$ is a mapping, $f^*: H^*\sY \to H^*\sX$ homomorphism of rings, and one has the important {\it projection formula}, 
\bean
f_*\left( f^*a \frown b\right) = a \frown f_*b
\eean 
Any $k$-dimensional subvariety $\sV$ of $\sX$ determines a class denoted $\mathrm {cl}(\sV)$ in 
$H_{2k}\sX$. This follows for example from the fact that $\sV$ can be triangulated to be an 
oriented 2$k$-circuit. If $f: \sX \to \sY$ is a morphism, and $f\left(\sV \right)= \mathcal W$, then 
\bean
f_*\mathrm {cl}(\sV)= \deg(\sV/\mathcal W)\mathrm {cl}(\mathcal W),
\eean 
where $\deg(\sV/\mathcal W)$ is defined as follows. If $\dim(\mathcal W) < \dim(\sV)$, then $\deg(\sV/\mathcal W)= 0$
If $\dim(\sV)= \dim (\mathcal W)$, there is an open $\mathcal W^*$ such that  $\sV \cap f^{-1} \left( \mathcal W^* \right) \to \mathcal W^*$ 
is a finite-fold topological covering, and $\deg(\sV/\mathcal W)$ is the number of sheets of 
this covering; algebraically, $\deg(\sV/\mathcal W)$ is the degree of the function field $R(\sV)$ of $\sV$
as a field extension of $R(\mathcal W)$.
If $\sX$ is nonsingular of dimension $n$, capping with $\mathrm{cl}\left( \sX\right)$ gives the {\it Poincare 
	duality} isomorphism 
\bean
H^p\sX \xrightarrow[\cong]{\frown \mathrm{cl}\left( \sX\right)  } H_{2n - p}\sX.
\eean 
In the nonsingular case, $H_*\sX = H^*\sX$ has an intersection product. If $A$ and $B$ are 
subvarieties of $\sX$ of dimensions $a$ and $b$, one may therefore define $A \cdot B$ in $H{2a + 2b - 2n}.\left( \sX\right)$  This product may be refined by using relative groups: 
\bean
\mathrm{cl}\left(A\right) \in H_{2a}\left(A \right) = H^{2n - 2a}\left(\sX , \sX \setminus A \right) 
\eean 
and similarly $\mathrm{cl}\left(B \right) \in H^{2n - 2b} \left(\sX, \sX \setminus B \right)$, so 
\bean
\mathrm{cl}\left( A\right) \smile \mathrm{cl}\left( B\right)\in  H^{4n - 2a - 2b}\left(\sX, \sX \setminus \left( A \cap B\right)  \right) \cong H_{4n - 2a - 2b}\left( A \cap B\right)
\eean
and thus  $A\cdot B$ lives  in $H_{4n - 2a - 2b}\left( A \cap B\right)$. Note that if the intersection is 
proper, this last group is free on the classes of irreducible components of  $A\cap B$, 
so this determines $A\cdot B$ as a cycle; in other words, this gives a topological 
construction of intersection multiplicities. 



Complex vector bundles $E$ in $\sX$ have {\it Chern classes} $c_j \in H^{2j}\left(\sX \right) $, satisfying: 
\begin{enumerate}
	\item [(i)] $c_0\left( E\right) = 1; ~ c_j\left(E \right) = 0$ if $j > \rank \left(E \right)$. 
	\item[	(ii)] If $f : \sY \to \sX, ~ c_j\left(f^*E \right)= f^*\left( c_j\left(E \right) \right)$.
	\item [(iii)] If $0 \hookto E' \hookto E \onto E''$ is an exact sequence, then
	$$
	c_j = \sum_{k + l = j} c_k \left(E' \right)\smile c_l \left(E'' \right). 
	$$ 
	\item [(iv)] If $L$ is an algebraic line bundle on $\sX$ and $s$ is a section of $L$ with 
	zero-scheme $D_s \neq \sX$, then 
	
	where cl([DJ) = Em,.01B),) if [Ds] = ??,.?. is the cycle of Ds. 
\end{enumerate}

\paragraph{TTTT}



Each $k$-dimensional complex variety $\sV$ has a cycle class ${cl}(\sV)$  in $H_{2k}\left( \sV\right)$, where 
$H_*$ denotes homology with locally finite supports (Borel-Moore homology). If $\sV$ is a subvariety of an $n$-dimensional complex manifold $\sX$, then $H_{2k}(\sV) \cong H^{2n - 2k} \left(\sX \setminus \sV \right)$ 
The resulting homomorphism from cycles to homology 
passes to algebraic equivalence. There results in particular a cycle map
\be
cl : A_*\left(\sX  \right) \to H_*\left( \sX\right) 
\ee
for complex schemes $\sX$, which is covariant for proper morphisms, and 
compatible with Chern classes of vector bundles. 
If $\sV$ and $\mathcal W$ are subvarieties of dimensions $k$ and $l$ of a non-singular $n$-dimensional variety $\sX$, a refined topological intersection product $cl\left(\sV \right)\cdot cl\left( \mathcal W\right)$   
is constructed in $H_{2m}(\sV \cap \mathcal W)$, $m = k + l-n$. If $cl^\sX (\sV)$is the class in 
$H^{2n - 2k}(\sX,\sX \setminus \sV)$ dual to $cl(\sV)$, and similarly for $cl^\sX(\mathcal W)$, then $cl(\sV)\dot(\mathcal W)$
is defined to be the class dual to 
$$
cl^\sX\left( \sV\right) \smile 	cl^\sX\left( \mathcal W\right)\in H^{2n - 2m}\left(\sX, \sX \setminus \sV \cap \mathcal W \right). 
$$
Borel-Moore homology can be defined using singular cohomology. If a 
space $\sX$ is imbedded as a closed subspace of $\R^n$, then 
\be\label{chow1_eqn}
H_j\left(\sX  \right) \cong H^{n-j}\left(\R^n, \R^n \setminus \sX \right) 
\ee
where the group on the right is relative singular cohomology with integer 
coefficients. More generally, if $\sX$ is a closed subspace of a space $\sY$, there are 
cap products 
\be\label{chow2_eqn}
H^j\left(\sY, \sY \setminus\sX \right) \otimes \xrightarrow{\frown}H_{k-j}\left(\sX \right). 
\ee
If $\sX$ is an oriented, connected, real $n$-manifold, then $H_n\left( \sY\right)$ is freely generated by 
a \textit{fundamental class} $\mu_\sY$, and capping with $\mu_\sY$ determines an isomorphism 
\be\label{chow3_eqn}
H^{n-j}\left(\sY, \sY \setminus \sX \right) \xrightarrow[\cong]{\frown \mu_\sY}H_{k-j}\left( \sX\right). 
\ee
When $\sY = \R^n$, this is the isomorphism of \eqref{chow1_eqn}. When $\sX = \sY$, \eqref{chow3_eqn} is the Poincar\'{e} duality isomorphism of $H^{n-j}\left(\sY \right)$  with $H_{j}\left(\sY \right)$. 
If $f : \sY \to \sX$ is a proper morphism, there are covariant homomorphisms 
\be\label{chow4_eqn}
f_* : H_{j}\left(\sX \right) \to H_{j}\left(\sY \right) 
\ee
If $j: \sU \to \sY$ is an open embedding, there are contravariant restriction homomorphisms
\be\label{chow5_eqn}
j^* : H_{p}\left(\sY \right) \to H_{p}\left(\sU \right). 
\ee
If $\sX$ is the complement of $\sU$ in $\sY$, $i: \sX\to \sY$ the closed embedding, there is a long exact sequence 
\be\label{chow6_eqn}
...\to  H_{p+1}\left(\sU \right) \to H_{p}\left(\sX \right)\xrightarrow{i_*} \H_{p}\left(\sY \right)\xrightarrow{j_*}H_{p}\left(\sU \right)\to H_{p-1}\left(\sX \right)\to .... 
\ee
If $\sX$ is a disjoint union of a finite number of spaces $\sX_1,..., \sX_m$, then 
\be\label{chow7_eqn}
H_{i}\left(\sX \right) = H_{i}\left(\sX_1 \right) \oplus ...\oplus H_{i}\left(\sX_m \right)
\ee 
There are evident compatibilities among these homomorphisms, which will be used without comment. One such is the equation  
\be\label{chow8_eqn}
\left( u \smile v \right) \frown a = j^*\left( u\right)\frown \left( v \frown a\right)  
\ee 
in $H_*\left( \sX \cap \mathcal W\right)$ , where $\sX \hookto \sY$, $~j:\mathcal W \to  \sY$ are closed embeddings, $u \in H^*(\sY, \sY\setminus \sX), ~v \in H^*(\sY, \sY- \mathcal W), ~a \in H_*\left( \sY\right)$. 
\begin{lemma}\cite{fulton:intersection}
	% Lemma 19.1.1. 
	If $\sX$ is an $n$-dimensional complex scheme, then $H^j(\sX) =\{0\}$ for 
	$i >2n$, and $H_{2n}\left(\sX \right) $ is a free Abelian group with one generator for each irreducible 
	component of $\sX$. 
\end{lemma}
\begin{definition}
	The generator of $H_{2n}\left(\sX \right)$ corresponding to an $n$-dimensional irreducible 
	component $\sX_i$, will be denoted $cl(\sX_i)$; it is determined by the fact that it 
	restricts to the fundamental class $\mu_{\sU_i}$ for any connected open subset $\sU_i$, of the 
	non-singular locus of $\sX_i$. More generally, if $\sV$ is a $k$-dimensional closed sub variety of a scheme $\sX$, define the \textit{cycle class} $cl_\sX(V)$ by 
	\be
	cl_\sX\left(\sV \right) \bydef i_* cl\left(\sV\right)\in H_{2k}\left( \sX\right) 
	\ee
	where $i$ is the inclusion of $\sV$ in $\sX$. When no confusion is likely, we may write $cl (\sV)$ 
	in place of $cl_\sX\left( V\right)$. It is proven in \cite{fulton:intersection}. For any $\sX$, there is a homomorphism denoted $cl$, or $cl_\sX$, 
	\bean
	A_*(\sX )\to H_*\left(\sX \right),\\
	\sum_i n_i \left[\sV_i\right] \mapsto \sum_i n_i cl\left(\sV_i\right).
	\eean 
\end{definition}
\begin{definition}\label{ad_ori_defn}
	Every regular (closed) embedding $i: \sV\hookto\sX$ of codimension $d$ has an \textit{orientation class}.
	\be\label{ad_ori_eqn}
	u_i = u_{\sV, \sX}\in H^{2d}\left(\sX, \sX \setminus \sV \right) 
	\ee 
\end{definition}
There is a long exact sequence of cohomology
\be
\begin{split}
	...\to  H^{p-1}\left(\sV ; \Z\right) \to H^{p}\left(\sX, \sX\setminus\sV ;\Z\right)\xrightarrow{i^*_p} H^{p}\left(\sX;\Z \right)\xrightarrow{j^*_p}H^{p}\left(\sV ; \Z\right)\to\\ \to H^{p+1}\left(\sX, \sX\setminus\sV ; \Z\right)\to .... 
\end{split}
\ee
There is an Abelian group homomorphism $cl: A^*\left( \sX\right)  \to H^*\left(\sX \right)$ such that if $\sV$ is an irreducible $k$-dimensional submanifold of $\sX$ then
\be
cl \left(\left[\sY\right] \right) = i^*_{2d}\left(u_{\sV, \sX} \right)\in H^{2d} \left(\sX \right)
\ee 


\begin{corollary}
	%19.2
	The mapping $cl: A^*\left( \sX\right)  \to H^*\left(\sX \right)$ is a homomorphism of graded rings, covariant for morphism of non-singular varieties. 
\end{corollary}

\section{Miscellany}
	

\subsection{Fundamental theorem of projective geometry}
\begin{defn}\cite{berger:geometryI}
	Let $\sV. \sV'$ be vector spaces over $K, K'$. a map $f: \sV \to \sV'$ is called {\it semilinear} if there exists an automorphism $\sigma :K \to K'$ such that
	\bean
	f\left(\la x + \mu y \right) = \sigma\left(\la \right) f\left( x\right) + \sigma\left(\mu \right) f\left( y\right) 
	\eean
	for all $x, y\in \sV$, $\la, \mu \in K$. If $\sX, \sX'$ are affine spaces over $K, K'$ a map $f: \sX \to \sX'$ is called {\it semiaffine} if there exists $a \in \sX$ such that $\overline f: \sX_a \to \sX_{f\left(a \right) }$ is semilinear.
	
\end{defn}
\begin{theorem}\cite{berger:geometryI}
Let $\sX$, $\sX'$ be affine spaces of same finite dimension $d \ge 2$. Let $f: \sX \to \sX'$ be a bijection which takes any three collinear points $a, b, c \in \sX'$ into  collinear points $f(a), f(b), f(c)\in \sX'$. Then $f$ is semiaffine
\end{theorem}
\begin{theorem}\label{fund_proj_thm}\cite{berger:geometryI}
Let both $\mathbb{P}\left( E\right)$,   $\mathbb{P}\left( E'\right)$ two projective spaces of equal dimension  $\ge 2$ over fields $K$ and $K'$. Let $f: \mathbb{P}\left( E\right)\cong \mathbb{P}\left( E'\right)$ be a set theoretic bijection such that for any three collinear points $a, b, c \in mathbb{P}\left( E\right)$ the points $f(a), f(b), f(c) \in \mathbb{P}\left( E\right)$ are collinear then there is a semilinear map $f : E \to E'$ with $f = \underline{ \hat f}$
\end{theorem}
